  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1cc98892-a56c-4648-9bdf-cd474f963476'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer1679659789144183997"><a href='https://amzn.to/2Wi7amb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wishlist</a> | <a></a><a href='https://diaryofdifference.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> | <a href='https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> | <a href='https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> | <a href='https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> | <a></a><a href='https://ko-fi.com/diaryofdifference' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ko-fi</a><br/><br/><b>Rosewood Chronicles</b><br/><br/>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2598018490' rel='nofollow noopener'>Undercover Princess</a> - ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2761943995' rel='nofollow noopener'>Princess in Practice</a> - ★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3586340629' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lost Princess</a> - TBR<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554713440i/27330968._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>I am lucky to have the best sister ever, who keeps giving me books I love! She gave me Undercover Princess for my birthday back in November last year, and I finally managed to get to it. Thank you, sis!</i><br/><br/>Even though Undercover Princess has great resemblance to The Princess Diaries and The Princess Protection Program, this book is unique in</span>
  <span id="freeText1679659789144183997" style="display:none"><a href="https://amzn.to/2Wi7amb" rel="nofollow noopener">Wishlist</a> | <a></a><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a></a><a href="https://ko-fi.com/diaryofdifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Ko-fi</a><br><br><b>Rosewood Chronicles</b><br><br>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2598018490" rel="nofollow noopener">Undercover Princess</a> - ★★★★★<br>#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2761943995" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess in Practice</a> - ★★★★<br>#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3586340629" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Princess</a> - TBR<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554713440i/27330968._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>I am lucky to have the best sister ever, who keeps giving me books I love! She gave me Undercover Princess for my birthday back in November last year, and I finally managed to get to it. Thank you, sis!</i><br><br>Even though Undercover Princess has great resemblance to The Princess Diaries and The Princess Protection Program, this book is unique in its own way, and the story is very different and positively surprising. I was in love with the characters and loved this book a lot. I will definitely be reading the second book of the series!<br><br>The story focuses on two main characters: <br><br><b>
  <i>* Lottie Pumpkin - the ordinary girl<br>* Ellie Wolf - the princess</i>
</b><br><br>And I wish it was all so easy. But you see, Lottie is an ordinary girl, she grew up in England and her mother passed away when she was little. Before she passes away, she gives Lottie a tiara for her birthday and makes her promise that she will always be brave. Lottie’s only goal in life is to attend Rosewood Hall, no matter what. And she makes it, with a scholarship. <br><br>On the other side, we have Ellie, the princess of Maradova. All she ever wants to be is ordinary, but she is surrounded by servants and shiny items. She wants to go to Rosewood Hall, only to avoid all her royal duties. And the only way of her parents letting this happen is if she attends the college undercover. <br><br>Then we have these two girls being roommates. A rumour spreads around the school and everyone thinks that Lottie is the princess. And in this whole mystery, the real princess is in danger, but no one must know that the real princess is Ellie. <b>And this is only the beginning.</b><br><br>The story is full of adventures and hilarious scenes, where we see Lottie and Ellie building their friendship, and trying to figure out the mystery behind all the threats they are receiving, all while they attend classes and go to parties like ordinary college girls. <br><br>While they play this game of swapping identities, they realise that this is more than a game, it is a lifestyle. And if Lottie is the undercover princess, she has to do everything to protect the real princess and her identity. Is this what she really wants? Is their friendship worth it? <br><br>There was a LGBT reference with a couple in this book, and maybe it was me, but I could also see a few sparks between Lottie and Ellie. I honestly expected something to happen between Lottie and Ellie's bodyguard. There were sparks though, so perhaps in the next book?<br><br>I loved how the partially-romantic scenes were building up to the real moment and made me want to read more. The writing skills this author has is truly amazing, and I praise her for it. It was a pleasure to read each chapter.<br><br><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1679659789144183997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2120839051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120839051" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120839051?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120839051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13342937302258426778">DNF at 50%<br/><br/>I think this is a major case of 'it's not me, it's you'. <br/><br/>Rosewood Chronicles tells the story of Lottie Pumpkin as she enters the privileged world of boarding schools at Rosewood Hall. Here she meets Ellie Wolf, secret princess of Maradova, and otherwise normal teenage girl. Together the two form a friendship as they fight to keep Ellie's true identity a secret - which might be more difficult than it sounds.<br/><br/>The writing for this was very clunky at best, with the descriptions and plot all</span>
  <span id="freeText13342937302258426778" style="display:none">DNF at 50%<br /><br />I think this is a major case of 'it's not me, it's you'. <br /><br />Rosewood Chronicles tells the story of Lottie Pumpkin as she enters the privileged world of boarding schools at Rosewood Hall. Here she meets Ellie Wolf, secret princess of Maradova, and otherwise normal teenage girl. Together the two form a friendship as they fight to keep Ellie's true identity a secret - which might be more difficult than it sounds.<br /><br />The writing for this was very clunky at best, with the descriptions and plot all over the place. There's no world building - I only have a vague idea of where Rosewood Hall actually is, and beyond that I know nothing of the wider world. Is it suppose to be similar to ours? Where is Maradova? Why does it appear like it's identical to England? The description of things also confused me. I wasn't really able to picture what Rosewood Hall looked like in my mind, although it did seem to have weird hidden passage ways/two way mirrors conveniently placed for eavesdropping?<br /><br />Ellie and Lottie. That weird bath scene near the beginning where Ellie is half naked? It's just...weird. And not something I would believe many women would do, let alone two fourteen year old girls. It was a bit creepy, and made me feel uncomfortable. In fact, their whole relationship in general was odd. They go from being immediate enemies (based entirely on the state of a bedroom) to extremely close friends in the space of seconds.<br /><br />I think I gave up around the the time the character of Jamie is introduced - mainly because he was really boring, with no apparent personality and with a really odd backstory. In fact, none of the characters are really described very well and because of this I had no interest in any of them.<br /><br />This may appeal to a much younger audience, who may be able to overlook these major discrepancies - unfortunately I couldn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13342937302258426778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer17203030456384541556">4.5* Harry Potter meets Cinderella, meets The Princess Diaries, meets The Princess Protection Programme (yes, that fab and totally underrated Demi Lovato/Selena Gomez movie) in Connie Glynn's wonderful debut novel, Undercover Princess. I'm painfully aware of how many 'meets etc.' I've just used but I promise they will *hopefully* make sense after you've read the book, which, of course, you definitely should do. Yet, even with these comparisons (of some of my favourite films, I should add), Under</span>
  <span id="freeText17203030456384541556" style="display:none">4.5* Harry Potter meets Cinderella, meets The Princess Diaries, meets The Princess Protection Programme (yes, that fab and totally underrated Demi Lovato/Selena Gomez movie) in Connie Glynn's wonderful debut novel, Undercover Princess. I'm painfully aware of how many 'meets etc.' I've just used but I promise they will *hopefully* make sense after you've read the book, which, of course, you definitely should do. Yet, even with these comparisons (of some of my favourite films, I should add), Undercover Princess is undoubtedly it's own unique story, full of imagination and wonder.<br /><br />Check out my full review for Undercover Princess here... <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://girlreading.co.uk/bookreviews/undercover-princess-by-connie-glynn-noodlerella-book-review/">http://girlreading.co.uk/bookreviews/...</a></span>

<div id="review_2182047950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2182047950" />
    <a title="beth ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72715251-beth"><img alt="beth ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600471872p2/72715251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2182047950?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="beth ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="beth ✨" href="/user/show/72715251-beth">beth ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141379852" href="/book/show/34514480-undercover-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72715251-beth?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2182047950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13660459074436138074"><b> Rating </b> - 3/3.5 stars.<br/><br/>I have never watched any of Connie's youtube videos and didn't realise she was a book tuber until I read a few comments before going into this book.<br/><br/>This book was okay. I didn't love it but I didn't hate it. It was a quick and easy read to get through and I finished it within two sittings.<br/><br/>I saw <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kate (Girl Reading's)</a> review and I have to agree with it being all of the things she mentioned. It was like reading a disney original movie/tv show in a book form. It reminded me of </span>
  <span id="freeText13660459074436138074" style="display:none"><b> Rating </b> - 3/3.5 stars.<br /><br />I have never watched any of Connie's youtube videos and didn't realise she was a book tuber until I read a few comments before going into this book.<br /><br />This book was okay. I didn't love it but I didn't hate it. It was a quick and easy read to get through and I finished it within two sittings.<br /><br />I saw <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate (Girl Reading's)</a> review and I have to agree with it being all of the things she mentioned. It was like reading a disney original movie/tv show in a book form. It reminded me of Princess Protection Programme and The Princess Diaries so much - which was good, as I am not ashamed to say how much I love them movies! - and it also had some small similarities to Harry Potter and many different fairytales.<br /><br />The characters were okay. I loved Ellie &amp; Lottie but I did have some issues with each of them. Ellie wasn't quite as 'rebellious' and 'crazy' as were told she was. I was kind of waiting for her personality to come out but it just didn't. Lottie was pretty cool but I had issues in how she treated her best friend from home. I don't wanna say too much else as I want this to be spoiler free but I did have issues with both. I didn't really care for any other character. Jamie was just...so...bland. I have no other word to describe him. I didn't care for him, he truly made me bored when he was there.<br /><br />The relationships were okay. Uh...so I know that Ellie &amp; Lottie are 'friends' but...I kind of shipped them together? I seriously did, I felt like I could feel some tension between them but I don't think that will be explored. There was a 'romance' kind of in this book but I truly didn't care for this what so ever. Truthfully, I only cared about the relationship between Ellie and Lottie. <br /><br />I think I would enjoy this more if I was younger and starting to read for the first time. It was enjoyable but I wasn't blown away. <br /><br />Confession: The cover is what made me truly pick up this book as it is absolutely stunning. Wow.<br /><br />I might pick up the next book but truthfully, I don't know if I am that bothered continuing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13660459074436138074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1904486494" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904486494" />
    <a title="Claire ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52966783-claire"><img alt="Claire ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490484695p2/52966783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904486494?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire ✨" href="/user/show/52966783-claire">Claire ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966783-claire?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966783-claire?shelf=rated-2-star">rated-2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966783-claire?shelf=genre-contemporary">genre-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966783-claire?shelf=advanced-reader-copy">advanced-reader-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966783-claire?shelf=great-concept-shoddy-execution">great-concept-shoddy-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52966783-claire?shelf=age-ya">age-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904486494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5035182479822773240"><i>UNDERCOVER PRINCESS is a fun, adventurous tale with charming main characters and an intriguing mystery, but its downfall is the underdeveloped supporting cast, juvenile prose, poor world-building and contrived plot.</i><br/><br/>This book is very obviously written by a YouTuber, and by that I mean, <b>someone given a book deal for their audience, not their penmanship.</b> The writing and plotting are messy and cringe-worthy, at times, despite how much love and heart there is in this novel.<br/><br/>I’m an absolute sucker for </span>
  <span id="freeText5035182479822773240" style="display:none"><i>UNDERCOVER PRINCESS is a fun, adventurous tale with charming main characters and an intriguing mystery, but its downfall is the underdeveloped supporting cast, juvenile prose, poor world-building and contrived plot.</i><br><br>This book is very obviously written by a YouTuber, and by that I mean, <b>someone given a book deal for their audience, not their penmanship.</b> The writing and plotting are messy and cringe-worthy, at times, despite how much love and heart there is in this novel.<br><br>I’m an absolute sucker for preppy boarding school mystery stories, so when I heard Glynn was writing THE ROSEWOOD CHRONICLES, I was hype immediately. I don’t religiously watch Glynn’s videos, but I do enjoy her content occasionally, and I was still hoping for this book to be a juicy read.<br><br>Unfortunately, this was me after finishing:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484796393ra/21754638.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The voice is juvenile,</b> unpractised and clunky. Very <i>tell, not show,</i> in places where showing would be more appropriate than telling, and because of it, the prose is <b>stilted, overexplains and filters constantly. </b>“Ellie did this. Jamie did that. Lottie felt this” pretty much explains the entire structure of the writing. Adverbs are rampant when there is usually a better verb that could capture the emotion of the speaker more efficiently.<br><br><b>Dialogue is jarring</b>, littered with amateur mistakes like spamming capslock for entire spoken sentences, or restating people’s names over and over again. <s><b>Inconsistency</b> in use of British or American spellings. <b>Incorrect grammar.</b></s><br><br>Characters often overreacted and it made melodrama more than good conflict. Some of the dynamics are just all out badly-written, most especially <b>the intimacy between Lottie and Ellie.</b> Like… stroking one another, nuzzling into their hair, taking icing off the other’s cheek with a finger and then licking it, nibbling one another. The problem isn't that they're love interests; the problem is that it seems like a rushed attempt at gradual romance.<br><br><s>(Note for publishers: send clean copies of your ARCs! Do you know how annoying it is to read actual copy-editing notes the middle of the text, like “change slung to strung” or “delete comma”?)</s><br><br><b>The plot is confusing and downright incoherent at times.</b> Lottie is somehow able to tell <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[by looking at a mirror in a painting that the school founder was a woman…? She also can’t sleep because of a piece of paper under her bed…? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Things like that had me more bewildered than intrigued, and there’s no meatier explanation with each situation to bridge the gap.<br><br>In addition, <b>plot points are contrived, convenient and lack foreshadowing.</b> I cannot fathom why Lottie and Ellie made such a big deal out of Binah's puzzles (an actual <i>maths</i> puzzle is in this book! Most bizarre thing I’ve seen in a novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1775650075?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">and I’m counting the weird font changes</a> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25760792.Timekeeper__Timekeeper___1_" title="Timekeeper (Timekeeper, #1) by Tara Sim" rel="nofollow noopener">TIMEKEEPER</a>). Isn't the current predicament more concerning, girls? I’d rather find out <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who’s sending me threatening library books and trying to curse me with paper <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, thanks.<br><br>Other plot conveniences include: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jamie randomly figuring out the maths problem; Anastacia being interrupted when she’s just about to tell Lottie something possibly plot-important; Priscilla’s workshop being held at Rosewood, rather than literally anywhere else in the world; bumping into Anastacia and all her things falling out from her bag. Only one person clocking that Ellie <i>Wolf</i> sounds like <i>Wolf</i>son. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>The climax, as such, was a total disappointment.</b> I didn’t fear the villain because the explanation behind their villainy was flimsy, and they made ‘amateur villain’ mistakes like divulging their evil scheme before they’d fully executed their plan and evaded getting caught.<br><br>One of the biggest problem was <b>the ‘magic’ wasn’t explained at all.</b> In a postscript from Glynn she explains that the fantastical nature of this series is merely atmospherical, of coincidence and fate, but that doesn't really make sense when there is literally <i>magic</i> that occurs that deliberately echoes fairy tales. Case and point, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a cursed piece of paper under a mattress that stops Lottie from sleeping à la The Princess and the Pea… <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Likewise, <b>the world-building of Maradova is poor.</b> A country somewhere close to Russia, the only explanation of its history is that it was once part of the British Empire but reclaimed independence and kept English as the main language. <b>This is a barebones explanation and not realistic.</b> Why wouldn’t Maradovans have their own accents, their own culture or traditions? At the moment, <b>the country is utterly indistinguishable from England,</b> and both Ellie and Jamie act exactly the same way that Lottie does, despite being from two different countries between them. It unfortunately seemed like a lazy world-building shortcut.<br><br><s><b>Lottie is basically a Noodlerella self-insert.</b> She adores fairy tales and Disney, always wears pink, has an obsession with princesses, and is a vegetarian. I guess I don’t really have a problem with this, but it doesn’t really speak for originality. As main character, Lottie had her sweet moments, but <b>most of the time her character was extremely and infuriatingly naïve, to the point where it defied basic logic.</b> She ignores all the signs that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Edmund was dodgy, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and even though Ellie and Jamie warn her, she completely ignores them and continues on.</s><br><br><s>To add to that, Lottie's view on vegetarianism came off as extremely preachy and self-rightious, and it really killed her whole "I'm good and kind" vibe.</s><br><br><b>Most of the supporting cast are unnecessary and underdeveloped.</b> There’s heads of year, sports captains and teacher’s assistants that are all named but have literally zero relevance. The teachers’ descriptions are all info-dumped in one go and it makes them forgettable. Lola and Micky could be mushed to create one character or removed entirely and nothing would change. Raphael, Saskia and Edmund are infuriatingly underdeveloped, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[especially the latter two. Edmund is blindingly obviously manipulating Lottie, whereas Saskia was only there to be a plot device. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Ellie, Jamie, Binah and Anastacia are the only side characters of importance, and even <b>they lack coherent descriptions of their appearance.</b> Jamie is at least half Pakistani and it’s not mentioned until after the midpoint of the book, by which point, I already had a mental image of his appearance. All it would take is Lottie to think “He had brown skin, possibly from Pakistan” or something. Heck, <b>even Lottie herself is poorly described;</b> it was at least twenty chapters before I learnt what colour hair she had.<br><br><s>Also, want to narrow my eyes at the fact that <b>the only confirmed Black character within the text smokes, swears and encourages trouble</b></s>… and <b>using food words to describe skin colours.</b> Yikes.<br><br>Despite all my problems, it was enjoyable on the surface. Like I said, <b>there’s a lot of heart,</b> and the main trio are adorable, funny and charming in their own way. <b>Lottie and Ellie have such a sweet friendship</b> (obviously blossoming into something else), and it’s a real driving force behind their shenanigans at the school.<br><br><b>I also loved Rosewood Hall, but I'm disappointed there wasn't a deeper look into it</b>. The secret passages, the houses, the lore; it was easy to be swept by it. The descriptions are lavish and rich and help you visualise the school well. Unfortunately, it wasn't enough. The series is called <i>The Rosewood Chronicles</i>; I shouldn't come out of it let down that there wasn't enough wonder and (strictly metaphorical) magic in such an illustrious boarding school.<br><br><b>
  <u>OVERALL?</u>
</b> This was honestly a lot better than my first read, but I think context absolutely helped (... as well as character art). However, still a very obvious first-novel-ever-written debut. Three stars for enjoyment, but two stars for storytelling technique.<br><br><i>eARC received from Penguin Random House via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. This title released 2nd November 2017.</i><br><br><b>EDIT 2nd November 2017:</b> Added some extra details.<br><br><b>EDIT 22nd November 2020:</b> I decided to reread this on whim, mostly to prepare for the upcoming <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51987874.Princess_at_Heart__The_Rosewood_Chronicles__4_" title="Princess at Heart (The Rosewood Chronicles #4) by Connie Glynn" rel="nofollow noopener">PRINCESS AT HEART</a>, in February 2021 and partly to see if I can finagle more hints about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3296731393" rel="nofollow noopener">my working theory</a> (spoilers on the link). My thoughts pretty much remain the same, so above is the edited version of my initial review, written in September 2017, altered to add clarity and succinctness. Some parts have been struck out as I no longer agree with my old opinion or it's no longer relevant (I first read the ARC version), however I've kept them here to keep the integrity of the original review.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437377608" rel="nofollow noopener">2: PRINCESS IN PRACTICE</a> || <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2756478912" rel="nofollow noopener">3: THE LOST PRINCESS</a> || <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3296731393" rel="nofollow noopener">4: PRINCESS AT HEART</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

I got 100 pages in and I wondered what the point of the story was, and it's a shame because it started off quite sweet.<br>Then <b>nothing. </b><br><br><br>All the characters were very clique, they weren't in the slightest bit interesting or entertaining, and very copy and paste from every middle grade/ya book ever. There was no development in the setting, characters, plot, anything. The writing was very simple and a bit lazy.<br><br>If you read this, I hope you enjoy it more than I did!</span>

<div id="review_2135580733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2135580733" />
    <a title="Stef White" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7936161-stef-white"><img alt="Stef White" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584791263p2/7936161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2135580733?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stef White" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stef White" href="/user/show/7936161-stef-white">Stef White</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2135580733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15676878159658585721">I recieved this book from Netgalley for an honest review. So Thank You Penguin Random House UK and obviously Connie Glynn.<br/><br/>Let me start off by saying I went into this book thinking it might be a little young for me. Being the ripe old age of 26, however that was so not the case this book engrossed me so much I read it in one sitting. I loved the character development, the relationship between Ellie and Lottie was just so cute. I adored the entire concept of this book.<br/>I was not expecting this book</span>
  <span id="freeText15676878159658585721" style="display:none">I recieved this book from Netgalley for an honest review. So Thank You Penguin Random House UK and obviously Connie Glynn.<br /><br />Let me start off by saying I went into this book thinking it might be a little young for me. Being the ripe old age of 26, however that was so not the case this book engrossed me so much I read it in one sitting. I loved the character development, the relationship between Ellie and Lottie was just so cute. I adored the entire concept of this book.<br />I was not expecting this book to have a mystery element but my gosh was it a good one.<br />Really excited to see where this story goes.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15676878159658585721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18851333-zili?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18851333-zili?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18851333-zili?shelf=drama">drama</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer12431908700734852849">I'm a conflicted about Undercover Princess because on one hand it's a nice boarding story but on the hand it's a little far fetched and loaded with certain YA tropes that I'm not a fan of.<br/><br/>I have to admit I wasn't aware of Connie Glynn as a YouTuber but I don't believe this would have had any impact on my experience of the book had I known beforehand. I'm very levelheaded with reviews and am willing to take it as it comes - if I like a book I like it.<br/><br/>Lottie Pumpkin (yes a cute name) finds herself</span>
  <span id="freeText12431908700734852849" style="display:none">I'm a conflicted about Undercover Princess because on one hand it's a nice boarding story but on the hand it's a little far fetched and loaded with certain YA tropes that I'm not a fan of.<br /><br />I have to admit I wasn't aware of Connie Glynn as a YouTuber but I don't believe this would have had any impact on my experience of the book had I known beforehand. I'm very levelheaded with reviews and am willing to take it as it comes - if I like a book I like it.<br /><br />Lottie Pumpkin (yes a cute name) finds herself drawn into a royal cover up when she's unknowingly roomed with the Crown Princess of Maradova. I liked the concept of a Princess trying to have a normal school experience away from the spotlight but I just couldn't fathom how NOBODY would have ever seen Ellie. <br /><br />I liked the friendship between Lottie and Ellie and kept thinking there was the chance it could blossom into more as it seemed a little flirtatious at times. <br /><br />I really would have liked to see more character development because it often felt a little flat. For example the villains didn't seem real because the jeopardy was lacking and a certain bad guy almost seemed like a spoof villain.<br /><br />I liked Jamie and would have loved to see more about him - more page time in the next instalment please!<br /><br />A lot happens in Undercover Princess so be prepared for lots of the usual teen romances and drama, as well as a hint of the mystical plus a big old royal showdown.<br /><br />3 Stars in my Sky!<br /><br />I received a copy in exchange for an honest review!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7630976365091302422">Cinderella, you will go to the ball! OK! There aren't any wicked step sisters, but there is a stepmother, a rinses and a ball in this YA adventure. However, most of the story actually takes place at Rosewood Hall, a prestigious boarding school that orphan Lottie Pumpkin has worked very hard to get into. She's the first student in twelve years to have a bursary scholarship to enable her to attend alongside the offspring of the elite and famous. <br/><br/>A misunderstanding on her first day leads others to </span>
  <span id="freeText7630976365091302422" style="display:none">Cinderella, you will go to the ball! OK! There aren't any wicked step sisters, but there is a stepmother, a rinses and a ball in this YA adventure. However, most of the story actually takes place at Rosewood Hall, a prestigious boarding school that orphan Lottie Pumpkin has worked very hard to get into. She's the first student in twelve years to have a bursary scholarship to enable her to attend alongside the offspring of the elite and famous. <br /><br />A misunderstanding on her first day leads others to assume she's the Crown Princess of Maradova - who is actually her room mate! So begins a story packed with intrigue, surprises and, yes, even a ball. As Lottie strives to keep working hard, the real princess, Ellie Wolf, is a rebellious influence and life will never be the same for any of them. Get ready for mischief, mayhem and even a kidnapping in this action packed story of teens in which I thoroughly enjoyed, even though I left my teens decades ago! I will certainly look forward to reading more in this series in future.<br /><br />i was gifted a copy of this book via NetGalley, without obligation. I chose to read it and this is my honest review after doing so.</span>

But, better late than never, right? <br/><br/><i>Undercover Princess</i> is not just a funny story about a girl who pretends to be a princess so that her friend who is <i>actually</i> a princess can be safe from harm. It's a story about a naïve but very intelligent girl whose heart is so big and pure that she allows herself to be in danger so that her fri</span>
  <span id="freeText5208248236491538560" style="display:none">How I wish this book had been written when I was fourteen and looking for a book about girls my age who fight for each other so they can become stronger individually. But, better late than never, right? <br /><br /><i>Undercover Princess</i> is not just a funny story about a girl who pretends to be a princess so that her friend who is <i>actually</i> a princess can be safe from harm. It's a story about a naïve but very intelligent girl whose heart is so big and pure that she allows herself to be in danger so that her friend isn't. It's a story that gloriously destroys stereotypes. It's a story that is also a reminder of how important true friendship can be and how difficult it is to keep it safe when times get hard. It's a story every girl should read.<br /><br /><i>Read the full review</i> <a href="https://parabataireviews.wordpress.com/2017/10/23/undercover-princess-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></span>

<div id="review_2361828882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2361828882" />
    <a title="Booklepuff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75799375-booklepuff"><img alt="Booklepuff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514811638p2/75799375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2361828882?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Booklepuff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Booklepuff" href="/user/show/75799375-booklepuff">Booklepuff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141379890" href="/book/show/37806858-undercover-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2361828882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8264196873686994442">Firstly this book for me only just scraped 1.5 Stars, Which barely ever happens! The cover of the arc itself was beautiful - this was one of my favourite parts about the book! But now the issues I had with it;<br/><br/>My copy was an ARC which I get means it’s not finished but the amount of spelling mistakes, missed words, cut off sentences, extra words and sentences that out right just didn’t make sense, made for really difficult reading! I’ve read many ARCs in the past and they’ve never been so poorly r</span>
  <span id="freeText8264196873686994442" style="display:none">Firstly this book for me only just scraped 1.5 Stars, Which barely ever happens! The cover of the arc itself was beautiful - this was one of my favourite parts about the book! But now the issues I had with it;<br /><br />My copy was an ARC which I get means it’s not finished but the amount of spelling mistakes, missed words, cut off sentences, extra words and sentences that out right just didn’t make sense, made for really difficult reading! I’ve read many ARCs in the past and they’ve never been so poorly read back over by the author!<br /><br />Writing style wise I thought it was clunky and undescriptive - rather than show us something through the writing, she would just tell us. I don’t have much of an idea what the characters look like, what Maradova or Rosewood Hall looks like either!<br /><br />Character wise I found Lottie incredibly annoying. She was naive and obsessed with being ‘kind, brave and unstoppable’ and once this was repeated again (and again and again) it really got on my nerves! I found the relationship between Lottie and Ellie quite weird, almost like more than friendship which is fine but if that is the case go with it, don’t just make weird stroking hair, licking cream of each other’s cheeks and snuggling up in bed scenes together without alluding to them being something more!<br /><br />I also thought the book would go off on strange tangents that weren’t necessary - like Binah’s puzzle, that was strange! How can you look at a picture and then say someone is actually female? And then nothing more came of it! <br /><br />I found the conclusion lacking as well - the person who was behind all the mystery and the villain of the novel was underdeveloped and there motivation behind it all seemed pretty flimsy too! <br /><br />Overall this book was a huge disappointment! Like all books from the start I go in without an opinion but from the first few chapters I wasn’t enjoying it and that didn’t change. It got slightly better by the end but everything else had annoyed me too much! I think that for a younger audience this book might be more appropriate or for someone that’s willing to look past all the cheesiness! Two good points - I did like Ellie and Jamie’s characters and wish they were more developed instead of Lottie!<br /><br />I don’t think it will be a series I will continue though unless something drastically changes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8264196873686994442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2163402455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7318265224929987514"><a href='https://shelovestoreaad.wordpress.com/2017/10/26/undercover-princess-by-connie-glynn-a-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Original Review Post</a><br/>First thing first i was really really excited to read this book. I mean come on princess's and private school and Mystery. It gave me such princess diaries, hex Hall and Hogwarts vibes. So when I got the email for reviewing I said count me the heck in.<br/><br/>Than when I got the book i got blown away by its prettiness. I love, love the arc. The front has a silhouette of a princess and has watercolors and has a big house castle silhouette on it. Anyway I am doing a sucky job of descr</span>
  <span id="freeText7318265224929987514" style="display:none"><a href="https://shelovestoreaad.wordpress.com/2017/10/26/undercover-princess-by-connie-glynn-a-review/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Original Review Post</a><br />First thing first i was really really excited to read this book. I mean come on princess's and private school and Mystery. It gave me such princess diaries, hex Hall and Hogwarts vibes. So when I got the email for reviewing I said count me the heck in.<br /><br />Than when I got the book i got blown away by its prettiness. I love, love the arc. The front has a silhouette of a princess and has watercolors and has a big house castle silhouette on it. Anyway I am doing a sucky job of describing it. But it's beautiful with a golden spine.<br />.<br />So yes in short i was EXCITED AND HAPPY as heck when I got it.<br />.<br />How let's get to story part and how that went. I think this story had a lot of potential. But it didn't deliver. Their were a lot of plot hole. And most of the things weren't quite impressive and left you underwhelmed. And it was also full of clichés.<br /><br /><b>Lets start with the main characters:</b><br /><br /> <b>Charlotte aka Lottie Pumpkin.</b> I just couldn't get her. She is supposed to be sensitive little soul. But she doesn't look hurt or even sensitive through out the book or like sad with an exception once or twice. And her point of selflessness for others is very HUH????!!!! Specially for a person she met 5 minutes ago and doesn't even know properly??!? Arent you supposed to be 14? i haven't seen a single 14 year old this stupid.<br />.<br /> The oh so <b>badass princess Ellie wolf.</b> Was so not badass. With the exception of dying her hair or like breaking in once or twice. Both of these characters were quite underwhelming.<br />.<br /> And their <b>friendship</b> I just could not get it. From being enemies to best friends in a hour?!?!! What how? How can you get so emotional and possessive or that friendly with someone so quickly to care that much about them? Their is this weird bath scene at the beginning and idk if it's how its told or Lottie describes it in such a weird way that it seem like it's something important. But I just don't see friends doing that together eh? And they are always like so intimate; stroking each other, taking icing off of the other ones face and nuzzling into the hair. I just don't know it was weird as heck their relationship. It would have been fine if it was a love interest but no where does the plot give away that. So I am left with the feeling *weird*.<br /><br /><br />The <b>plot</b> is all over the place. And sometimes makes so sense. There are so many different things thrown in into the mix that you have no clue of and what they are leading too and in the end some of them aren't even explained. For example Bina's puzzle, idk what It was about?? what it was for? And why she gave them it? It literally isn't even explained.<br />Their are so many different elements thrown into the mix that you can't help but wonder is this contemporary or is this fantasy? What exactly is this story? Their is some weird magic thing/storyline placed in between but even that isn't explained properly.<br /><br /><br />The <b>world</b> building is so poor. We don't know much about Maradova. It isn't established properly. Nor are it's customs. It was supposed to take place in Russia? And the language they speak is English they don't use their own dialect?!?!?!? Or have an accents or traditions?!!?!?!?! <br /><br /><b>Other characters.</b> Oh my god they are such a meh point; all of them. Most of them are so unnecessary and almost all of them are underdeveloped. Almost to the point they are just names. They have no relevance to the story other than two too three non story building cameos. Even the characters that bring something to the stories and have more interaction are just so personality less and meh. Jamie's has a back story toward the end and it's so odd and weird and out of place like what? Their is a stepmother thing going on but even that isn't explained. It's basically a lot of confusion and unbelievable stuff happening.<br /><br /><br /><b>Everything happens so fast. It unreal.</b><br /><br />Like this just being to happen and than abruptly end. They don't have a time to start , play/pan out and than end it's just oh this happened oh now this happened. Things aren't explained through out the story they just HAPPENs.<br />.<br />.<br /><b>The villains. </b> Omg all of them are so lame. And the whole mystery through out the story get more annoying by that point. Because half the villains that are supposed to be villainous or are suspects you don't know why they were doing that thing. Because no where was it explained. And the two that were. God eh? I didn't even get any thrill from it what do ever.<br />.<br />.<br />The <b>*writing*</b> I don't think I am a fan of it. It was too all over the place. No sense of direction. I think she just wanted to chuck every concept she found interesting into the story. She has 5000 plots going on and half of them she abandons in between and you are like what? And also. A lot of things about Lottie are basically the writer herself : aka her love for pink, fairy tales, being a vegetarian. *groans*<br />.<br />.<br /><b>So</b><br />This book had a lot and lot of potential as I said in the beginning. But it wasn't utilized. This book suffered a lot because their was not a clear direction. And I would have loved it if it was just about Rosewood Hall but it was just all over. The character had no personalities. And over all the book had no point in it where it did wow me.<br />Maybe a younger audience might like it and may able to overlook all the in-discrepancies but i don't think proper ya reader will enjoy this much.<br />I am sorry to say this one wasn't for me sadly.<br />.<br /><b>
  Thank you to Penguin Random House UK for the arc.
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7318265224929987514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2146932388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2146932388" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27151715-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513668062p2/27151715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2146932388?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/27151715-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=2017-releases-read">2017-releases-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2146932388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2785823623684441181">Okay. That’s how I would describe this book for me. It was simply: <b>okay</b>.<br/><br/>I didn’t dislike this book but neither did I love it. The plot was okay, it did have its moments where I will happily admit to being interested and I read the book fairly quickly but it just didn’t scream ‘READ ME’ or have anything that I found particularly gripping. In fact what the plot did for me was leave lots of unanswered questions and one of those was “Why did Lottie so desperately want to go to Rosewood Hall?”<br/><br/>I also </span>
  <span id="freeText2785823623684441181" style="display:none">Okay. That’s how I would describe this book for me. It was simply: <b>okay</b>.<br /><br />I didn’t dislike this book but neither did I love it. The plot was okay, it did have its moments where I will happily admit to being interested and I read the book fairly quickly but it just didn’t scream ‘READ ME’ or have anything that I found particularly gripping. In fact what the plot did for me was leave lots of unanswered questions and one of those was “Why did Lottie so desperately want to go to Rosewood Hall?”<br /><br />I also felt like the plot went from being super simple to having lots going on all at once rather than having one or two things happening that were really well developed which I think would have resulted in us seeing more layered characters too. I think it’s important for me to point out here that this book isn’t boring, lots happens and some readers will have loved the way it is written, I just really like layers and depth and this was definitely more of a fairytale (I appreciate this is probably intentional!)<br /><br />As for the characters, I’ve kind of touched on this above but I just felt they were quite flat. I really love a flawed, layered character that I can get to really know but although I felt that I liked most of the characters in this book, I got to the end and still didn’t really feel I knew them as well as I would have liked. If I was asked to describe their personalities I would have a really hard time doing it. Ellie is supposed to be this super rebellious Princess but she didn’t feel that rebellious to me, Lottie was adorable and very Disney Princess-like but what on earth happened to Ollie?! This really pained me because at the beginning Ollie and Lottie are super best friends, then she goes off to school and just forgets all about him. Granted she doesn’t have her phone but, HELLO, write a letter? I just felt like their friendship was totally just forgotten about and then something had to quickly be written back in at the end to acknowledge Ollie.<br /><br />I think the best way for me to end this review is to sum up my feelings and that goes a bit like this… <i>Undercover Princess</i> is a fluffy, light and Disney-like read that plenty of readers will love but if you are looking for a complex plot and layered characters, this won’t be the book for you. A lovely read and a GORGEOUS cover (had to slip that in…) but for me this book will be easily forgettable.<br /><br /><i>Thanks to NetGalley, Penguin and Connie Glynn for my advanced copy in exchange for a fair and honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2785823623684441181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2121900168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121900168" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60880871-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512949339p2/60880871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2121900168?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/60880871-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2121900168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8383077068627993345">It would be unfair to call this a book "review" - it's entirely unprofessional, incredibly biased, far too rambly and not at all critical because I'm still viewing this world through rose-tinted glasses. But I don't want to find fault in it, partially because I want to enjoy this at 21 as much as I'd enjoy it at 15, and partially because finding fault in it would take far too much effort on my part - it's wonderful. <br/><br/>The book isn't officially released until the first week of November, so I natura</span>
  <span id="freeText8383077068627993345" style="display:none">It would be unfair to call this a book "review" - it's entirely unprofessional, incredibly biased, far too rambly and not at all critical because I'm still viewing this world through rose-tinted glasses. But I don't want to find fault in it, partially because I want to enjoy this at 21 as much as I'd enjoy it at 15, and partially because finding fault in it would take far too much effort on my part - it's wonderful. <br /><br />The book isn't officially released until the first week of November, so I naturally can't post any spoilers or say too much, but let me say this; it's perfectly whimsical without demanding too much suspension of disbelief, because princesses exist, and boarding schools exist, and the characters are so well developed that it truly feels like they exist too. I never went to boarding school masquerading as an unannounced princess, yet if you changed some names and hair colours around there are passages in this book that reflect so much of what my life was as a 14 year old. The two main characters, Ellie and Lottie, talk about each other in a way that makes my heart so warm. All else aside, all conflict and fantasy and tiaras ignored, Connie's written a story about the importance of female friendship, the importance of people raising each other up, and when it starts to become painful to look at the news in a world that's supposed to be tolerant and forward thinking and progressive, this is the escape I've been needing. During the reading I watched at Summer in the City, Connie (this book's wonderful, wonderful author) said something that stuck with me, which is that she's a firm believer in being friends with people who bring out the best in you, and in trying to bring out the best in other people. This is a story about two teenage girls doing just that for each other, and it scares me a little that I've never read that before.<br /><br />I am in love with all that this book is, all that it represents, all the friendships I've created and happiness I've shared in just by scoring a proof copy. Knowing that this is just the start of my adventures alongside these characters is INCREDIBLE. Do yourself a favour and read and laugh and love this book as much as I do, please.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8383077068627993345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2132737965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2132737965" />
    <a title="Andrea Way" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45613003-andrea-way"><img alt="Andrea Way" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453748878p2/45613003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2132737965?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea Way" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea Way" href="/user/show/45613003-andrea-way">Andrea Way</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2132737965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16376732128426337132">2.5 stars. ***ARC Review from Netgalley and the publisher***<br/><br/>Sorry not one for me. This was a book that had an interesting premise and the friendship part was done well. But had way to many YA tropes for me. I think if I were younger I might have enjoyed this but I found myself skipping parts just to get to the end.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2166894588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2166894588" />
    <a title="Hannah " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14766427-hannah"><img alt="Hannah " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580576639p2/14766427.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2166894588?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah " href="/user/show/14766427-hannah">Hannah </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=first-time-read">first-time-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=not-as-expected">not-as-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=read-in-under-24-hours">read-in-under-24-hours</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=2-and-a-half-stars">2-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14766427-hannah?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2166894588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5086404170245698319"><i> I received this book via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review </i><br/><br/><b> Edit 30.10.17 actual rating 2.5 </b><br/><br/>This is a cute story of friendship intertwined with a decent bit of mystery (albeit with an unsatisfying reveal), which is enough to keep the reader guessing and the plot moving forward. Lottie, Jamie and Ellie were all likeable main characters and their relationships were generally well written and explored nicely but I don't really understand Lottie and Ellie's friendship/relationship/whatever</span>
  <span id="freeText5086404170245698319" style="display:none"><i> I received this book via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review </i><br /><br /><b> Edit 30.10.17 actual rating 2.5 </b><br /><br />This is a cute story of friendship intertwined with a decent bit of mystery (albeit with an unsatisfying reveal), which is enough to keep the reader guessing and the plot moving forward. Lottie, Jamie and Ellie were all likeable main characters and their relationships were generally well written and explored nicely but I don't really understand Lottie and Ellie's friendship/relationship/whatever it was. They were too physically close- with cuddling up under the covers stroking each other's faces and a very weird section of playful nibbling- to just be friends but no romantic relationship was explored so I genuinely have no idea what their relationship was. <br /><br />Overall I quite enjoyed it and will keep an eye out for the sequel as I think there is potential- there is a lot of action and drama in here as well as some genuinely touching friendships. I do have a few issues with it though:<br /><br />My main issue with this book is that it claims to be YA when it just isn't. It's a really good middle grade read, but the writing and characters are too juvenile to put it in the YA age bracket for me. There are moments where Lottie's thoughts verge on ridiculous <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Edmund must have an evil twin because he's behaving differently- what!?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and others where she figures out ridiculously difficult clues with far too much ease <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ working out the school founder had been born a woman because he was holding a mirror in a painting  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, why on earth was this never mentioned again? Basically, I would have enjoyed this a lot more if I'd gone into it expecting a middle grade novel, because it's a decent example of one.<br /><br />The descriptions are not done particularly well either, I'm not sure what Lottie looks like at all and Jamie being Pakistani wasn't mentioned until at least 75%, that's a pretty crucial description to miss. The only character I can actually picture is Ellie. Side note: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ how was it that only Anastasia noticed that Eleanor Wolfson and Ellie Wolf might have been the same person?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I understand almost nothing about Maradova- where is is, what it looks like etc, I can only tell you that it's cold there. Rosewood is fairly vivid though and I enjoyed the descriptions of the school. As this is a contemporary story with no magic, there were bits that confused me a lot- the reason behind Lottie's lack of sleep makes no sense in a non-magical world and there were elements of the school clearly ripped from Hogwarts (understandable in terms of world building but again makes little to no sense in the contemporary setting).<br /><br />Lottie's home life is not explored well. She basically abandons her best friend with a couple of tears then forgets about him forever more, which feels uncomfortable as they have been friends for life and he was there for her through her mother's death. She forgets about Ollie as soon as she meets Ellie and fails to explain anything to him- I will be genuinely amazed if he features in the series again.<br />Lottie also doesn't grieve for her mother appropriately- there are a couple of off hand comments clearly supposed to illicit sympathy that did nothing for me at all. <br /><br />The plot moves far too quickly and it felt like we went from Christmas to Summer in the span of maybe 30 pages? <br /><br />Also, I was not a fan of the very thinly veiled preachy comments about vegetarianism- obviously being a vegetarian is a totally valid choice and I have a lot of respect for people who do so- but comments about how eating animals isn't very 'princessy' felt both out of place and a bit preachy. Particularly the description of 'pigs wrapped in a blanket of their own flesh' was uncomfortable. It is possible to make characters vegetarian/vegan without these unnecessary comments. This is obviously only a very small thing but I found it incredibly irritating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5086404170245698319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of The Princess Diaries</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8803703-nicola?shelf=arc">arc</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2124664283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17488673430347337952"><i>Undercover Princess</i> combines royalty, a boarding school setting, puzzles and mysteries and creates something really fun. <br/><br/>Lottie and Ellie are polar opposites but quickly bond and become inseparable when some school gossip gets out of hand and they find a solution that works for both of them. I liked their friendship and the overall focus that was placed on female friendships throughout the book. Whilst there is a little romance (including LGBT), I liked that friendship was at the forefront and h</span>
  <span id="freeText17488673430347337952" style="display:none"><i>Undercover Princess</i> combines royalty, a boarding school setting, puzzles and mysteries and creates something really fun. <br /><br />Lottie and Ellie are polar opposites but quickly bond and become inseparable when some school gossip gets out of hand and they find a solution that works for both of them. I liked their friendship and the overall focus that was placed on female friendships throughout the book. Whilst there is a little romance (including LGBT), I liked that friendship was at the forefront and how it’s important to be a good friend. <br /><br />Unfortunately I also had a few problems with the book. There are a lot of the usual YA cliches and the writing isn’t perfect. The world-building is lacking in some places and there are elements that aren’t fully explained at all. It is a contemporary book but there are a few “magical” instances that aren’t properly developed or explained. <br /><br />Is it perfect? No. But if you can look past the cliches and the flaws, there is a warm and charming story to be found here.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9913162960946655876" style="display:none">So I've written a review before but whilst reading again i have noticed some more things.<br />You can tell it is a first book but it is by far not a terrible one, to the people moaning the first Harry Potter wasn't great but it improved.<br />I saw a review moaning about not enough character development from Ollie but what i think is Ollie will have more importance later in the series. <div id="review_2241446863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2241446863" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7501681-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468004725p2/7501681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2241446863?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/7501681-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/36502170-undercover-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2241446863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16116515217096481118">This review was also posted on my blog <a href='https://tecsielity.wordpress.com/2018/02/07/book-review-undercover-princess/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tecsielity</a>.<br/><br/>It’s been a while since I read something nice and light like this. I had somehow assumed the main characters would be a bit older teens though so it took me a moment to get used to the fact that they’re actually 14!<br/><br/>Undercover Princess was a little weird to me in that I actually enjoyed it but it also had some obvious issues, like the writing not being that great. Lottie and Ellie’s friendship was really sweet I kinda got the vibe that it may deve</span>
  <span id="freeText16116515217096481118" style="display:none">This review was also posted on my blog <a href="https://tecsielity.wordpress.com/2018/02/07/book-review-undercover-princess/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tecsielity</a>.<br /><br />It’s been a while since I read something nice and light like this. I had somehow assumed the main characters would be a bit older teens though so it took me a moment to get used to the fact that they’re actually 14!<br /><br />Undercover Princess was a little weird to me in that I actually enjoyed it but it also had some obvious issues, like the writing not being that great. Lottie and Ellie’s friendship was really sweet I kinda got the vibe that it may develop into a more romantic direction eventually. Ellie was a fun character even though it was a little strange that she seemed to get away with pretty much all rule breaking she did when people didn’t even know she was the actual princess. Lottie was also pretty relatable in some situations, like when she tried to correct the whole princess thing in the beginning but everybody talked over her. I really hated how she kept keeping secret after secret just for the sake of plot after she and Ellie had agreed multiple times they wouldn’t do that!<br /><br />Some things felt a little flat, for example all we really know about Ellie’s home country is that their original language is some form of Russian except everybody there speaks English anyway. Most side characters – even important ones – were pretty much just names with maybe one detail attached to them. Jamie could have been a really cool character but Lottie was somehow only obsessed with knowing how he got his job and never really tried to learn anything else about him.<br /><br />Lottie’s home situation really bothered me because they barely mentioned her having a dad and just living with her stepmother who didn’t seem to care about her at all sounded really weird. The only person to ask after her during the whole school year was her friend Ollie! I guess it was supposed to be a fairy tale evil stepmother situation…<br /><br />Despite all the little issues Undercover Princess was still a quick, easy read that made me feel happy feels. In my mind everything in the book was colored pink.<br /><br />Side note: I watched a couple of the author’s Youtube videos about the book and was surprised to learn the whole house thing in boarding schools is apparently not just a Harry Potter thing.</span>

          </span>
        </div>
